64→ * Given a base64 NUL-terminated string at src, decode it and return a\n    65→ * pointer in *outptr to a newly allocated memory area holding decoded\n    66→ * data. Function\n    69→ * output shall not be considered valid unless CURLE_OK is returned.\n    70→ *\n    71→ * When decoded data length is 0, returns NULL in *outptr.\n    72→ *\n    73→ * @unittest: 1302\n    74→ */\n    75→CURLcode Curl_base64_decode(const char *src,\n    76→                            unsigned char **outptr, size_t *outlen)\n    77→{\n    78→  size_t srclen = 0;\n    79→  size_t padding = 0;\n    80→  size_t i;\n    81→  size_t numQuantums;\n    82→  size_t fullQuantums;\n    83→  size_t rawlen = 0;\n    84→  unsigned char *pos;\n    85→  unsigned char *newstr;\n    86→  unsigned char lookup[256];\n    87→\n    88→  *outptr = NULL;\n    89→  *outlen = 0;\n    90→  srclen = strlen(src);\n    91→\n    92→  /* Check the length of the input string is valid */\n    93→  if(!srclen || srclen % 4)\n    94→    return CURLE_BAD_CONTENT_ENCODING;\n    95→\n    96→  /* srclen is at least 4 here */\n    97→  while(src[srclen - 1 - padding] == '=') {\n    98→    /* count padding characters */\n    99→    padding++;\n   100→    /* A maximum of two = padding characters is allowed */\n   101→    if(padding > 2)\n   102→      return CURLE_BAD_CONTENT_ENCODING;\n   103→  }\n   104→\n   105→  /* Calculate the number of quantums */\n   106→  numQuantums = srclen / 4;\n   107→  fullQuantums = numQuantums - (padding ? 1 : 0);\n   108→\n   109→  /* Calculate the size of the decoded string */\n   110→  rawlen = (numQuantums * 3) - padding;\n   111→\n   112→  /* Allocate our buffer including room for a null-terminator */\n   113→  newstr = malloc(rawlen + 1);\n   114→  if(!newstr)\n   115→    return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   116→\n   117→  pos = newstr;\n   118→\n   119→  memset(lookup, 0xff, sizeof(lookup));\n   120→  memcpy(&lookup['+'], decodetable, sizeof(decodetable));\n   121→  /* replaces\n   122→  {\n   123→    unsigned char c;\n   124→    const unsigned char *p = (const unsigned char *)base64encdec;\n   125→    for(c = 0;    /* Point to padding string. */\n   195→\n   196→  *outptr = NULL;\n   197→  *outlen = 0;\n   198→\n   199→  if(!insize)\n   200→    insize = strlen(inputbuff);\n   201→\n   202→  base64data = output = malloc((insize + 2) / 3 * 4 + 1);\n   203→  if(!output)\n   204→    return CURLE_OUT_OF_MEMORY;\n   205→\n   206→  while(insize >= 3) {\n   207→    *output++ = table64[ in[0] >> 2 ];\n   208→    *output++ = table64[ ((in[0] & 0x03) << 4) | (in[1] >> 4) ];\n   209→    *output++ = table64[ ((in[1] & 0x0F) << 2) | ((in[2] & 0xC0) >> 6) ];\n   210→    *output++ = table64[ in[2] & 0x3F ];\n   211→    insize -= 3;\n   212→    in += 3;\n   213→  }\n   214→  if(insize) {\n   215→    /* this is only one or two bytes now */\n   216→    *output++ = table64[ in[0] >> 2 ];\n   217→    if(insize == 1) {\n   218→      *output++ = table64[ ((in[0] & 0x03) << 4) ];\n   219→      if(*padstr) {\n   220→        *output++ = *padstr;\n   221→        *output++ = *padstr;\n   222→      }\n   223→    }\n   224→    else {\n   225→      /* insize == 2 */\n   226→      *output++ = table64[ ((in[0] & 0x03) << 4) | ((in[1] & 0xF0) >> 4) ];\n   227→      *output++ = table64[ ((in[1] & 0x0F) << 2) ];\n   228→      if(*padstr)\n   229→        *output++ = *padstr;\n   230→    }\n   231→  }\n   232→\n   233→  /* Zero terminate */\n   234→  *output = '\\0';\n   235→\n   236→  /* Return the pointer to the new data (allocated memory) */\n   237→  *outptr = base64data;\n   238→\n   239→  /* Return the length of the new data */\n   240→  *outlen = output - base64data;\n   241→\n   242→  return CURLE_OK;\n   243→}\n   244→\n   245→/*\n   246→ * Curl_base64_encode()\n   247→ *\n   248→ * Given a pointer to an input buffer and an input size, encode it and\n   249→ * return a pointer in *outptr to a newly allocated memory area holding\n   250→ * encoded data. The Domain Attribute says:\n   * For example, if the value of the Domain attribute is\n   * \"example.com\", the user agent will include the cookie in the Cookie\n   * header when making HTTP requests to example.com, www.example.com, and\n   * www.corp.example.com.\n   */\n  if(hostname_len == cookie_domain_len)\n    return TRUE;\n  if('.' == *(hostname + hostname_len - cookie_domain_len))\n    return TRUE;\n  return FALSE;\n}\n\n/*\n * matching cookie path and url path\n * RFC6265 5.1.4 Paths and Path-Match\n */\nstatic bool pathmatch(const char *cookie_path, const char *request_uri)\n{\n  size_t cookie_path_len;\n  size_t uri_path_len;\n  char *uri_path = NULL;\n  char *pos;\n  bool ret = FALSE;\n\n  /* cookie_path must not have last '/' separator. ex: /sample */\n  cookie_path_len = strlen(cookie_path);\n  if(1 == cookie_path_len) {\n    /* cookie_path must be '/' */\n    return TRUE;\n  }\n\n  uri_path = strdup(request_uri);\n  if(!uri_path)\n    return FALSE;\n  pos = strchr(uri_path, '?');\n  if(pos)\n    *pos = 0x0;\n\n  /* #-fragments are already cut off! */\n  if(0 == strlen(uri_path) || uri_path[0] != '/') {\n    strstore(&uri_path, \"/\", 1);\n    if(!uri_path)\n      return FALSE;\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * here, RFC6265 5.1.4 says\n   *  4. Output the characters of the uri-path from the first character up\n   *     to, but not including, the right-most %x2F (\"/\").\n   *  but URL path /hoge?fuga=xxx means /hoge/index.cgi?fuga=xxx in some site\n   *  without redirect.\n   *  Ignore this algorithm because /hoge is uri path for this case\n   *  (uri path is not /).\n   */\n\n  uri_path_len = strlen(uri_path);\n\n  if(uri_path_len < cookie_path_len) {\n    ret = FALSE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* not using checkprefix() because matching should be case-sensitive */\n  if(strncmp(cookie_path, uri_path, cookie_path_len)) {\n    ret = FALSE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* The cookie-path and the uri-path are identical. */\n  if(cookie_path_len == uri_path_len) {\n    ret = TRUE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  /* here, cookie_path_len < uri_path_len */\n  if(uri_path[cookie_path_len] == '/') {\n    ret = TRUE;\n    goto pathmatched;\n  }\n\n  ret = FALSE;\n\npathmatched:\n  free(uri_path);\n  return ret;\n}\n\n/*\n * Return the top-level domain, for optimal hashing.\n */\nstatic const char *get_top_domain(const char * const domain, size_t *outlen)\n{\n  size_t len = 0;\n  const char *first = NULL, *last;\n\n  if(domain) {\n    len = strlen(domain);\n    last = memrchr(domain, '.', len);\n    if(last) {\n      first = memrchr(domain, '.', (last - domain));\n      if(first)\n        len -= (++first - domain);\n    }\n  }\n\n  if(outlen)\n    *outlen = len;\n\n  return first? first: domain;\n}\n\n/* Avoid C1001, an \"internal error\" with MSVC14 */\n#if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\n#pragma optimize(\"\", off)\n#endif\n\n/*\n * A case-insensitive hash for the cookie domains.\n */\nstatic size_t cookie_hash_domain(const char *domain, const size_t len)\n{\n  const char *end = domain + len;\n  size_t h = 5381;\n\n  while(domain < end) {\n    h += h << 5;\n    h ^= Curl_raw_toupper(*domain++);\n  }\n\n  return (h % COOKIE_HASH_SIZE);\n}\n\n#if defined(_MSC_VER) && (_MSC_VER == 1900)\n#pragma optimize(\"\", on)\n#endif\n\n/*\n * Hash this domain.\n */\nstatic size_t cookiehash(const char * const domain)\n{\n  const char *top;\n  size_t len;\n\n  if(!domain || Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain))\n    return 0;\n\n  top = get_top_domain(domain, &len);\n  return cookie_hash_domain(top, len);\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie path sanitize\n */\nstatic char *sanitize_cookie_path(const char *cookie_path)\n{\n  size_t len;\n  char *new_path = strdup(cookie_path);\n  if(!new_path)\n    return NULL;\n\n  /* some stupid site sends path attribute with '\"'. */\n  len = strlen(new_path);\n  if(new_path[0] == '\\\"') {\n    memmove(new_path, new_path + 1, len);\n    len--;\n  }\n  if(len && (new_path[len - 1] == '\\\"')) {\n    new_path[--len] = 0x0;\n  }\n\n  /* RFC6265 5.2.4 The Path Attribute */\n  if(new_path[0] != '/') {\n    /* Let cookie-path be the default-path. */\n    strstore(&new_path, \"/\", 1);\n    return new_path;\n  }\n\n  /* convert /hoge/ to /hoge */\n  if(len && new_path[len - 1] == '/') {\n    new_path[len - 1] = 0x0;\n  }\n\n  return new_path;\n}\n\n/*\n * Load cookies from all given cookie files (CURLOPT_COOKIEFILE).\n *\n * NOTE: OOM or cookie parsing failures are ignored.\n */\nvoid Curl_cookie_loadfiles(struct Curl_easy *data)\n{\n  struct curl_slist *list = data->set.cookielist;\n  if(list) {\n    Curl_share_lock(data, CURL_LOCK_DATA_COOKIE, CURL_LOCK_ACCESS_SINGLE);\n    while(list) {\n      struct CookieInfo *newcookies =\n        Curl_cookie_init(data, list->data, data->cookies,\n                         data->set.cookiesession);\n      if(!newcookies)\n        /*\n         * Failure may be due to OOM or a bad cookie; both are ignored\n         * but only the first should be\n         */\n        infof(data, \"ignoring failed cookie_init for %s\", list->data);\n      else\n        data->cookies = newcookies;\n      list = list->next;\n    }\n    Curl_share_unlock(data, CURL_LOCK_DATA_COOKIE);\n  }\n}\n\n/*\n * strstore\n *\n * A thin wrapper around strdup which ensures that any memory allocated at\n * *str will be freed before the string allocated by strdup is stored there.\n * The intended usecase is repeated assignments to the same variable during\n * parsing in a last-wins scenario. The caller is responsible for checking\n * for OOM errors.\n */\nstatic void strstore(char **str, const char *newstr, size_t len)\n{\n  DEBUGASSERT(newstr);\n  DEBUGASSERT(str);\n  free(*str);\n  *str = Curl_memdup(newstr, len + 1);\n  if(*str)\n    (*str)[len] = 0;\n}\n\n/*\n * remove_expired\n *\n * Remove expired cookies from the hash by inspecting the expires timestamp on\n * each cookie in the hash, freeing and deleting any where the timestamp is in\n * the past.  If the cookiejar has recorded the next timestamp at which one or\n * more cookies expire, then processing will exit early in case this timestamp\n * is in the future.\n */\nstatic void remove_expired(struct CookieInfo *cookies)\n{\n  struct Cookie *co, *nx;\n  curl_off_t now = (curl_off_t)time(NULL);\n  unsigned int i;\n\n  /*\n   * If the earliest expiration timestamp in the jar is in the future we can\n   * skip scanning the whole jar and instead exit early as there won't be any\n   * cookies to evict.  If we need to evict however, reset the next_expiration\n   * counter in order to track the next one. In case the recorded first\n   * expiration is the max offset, then perform the safe fallback of checking\n   * all cookies.\n   */\n  if(now < cookies->next_expiration &&\n      cookies->next_expiration != CURL_OFF_T_MAX)\n    return;\n  else\n    cookies->next_expiration = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n\n  for(i = 0; i < COOKIE_HASH_SIZE; i++) {\n    struct Cookie *pv = NULL;\n    co = cookies->cookies[i];\n    while(co) {\n      nx = co->next;\n      if(co->expires && co->expires < now) {\n        if(!pv) {\n          cookies->cookies[i] = co->next;\n        }\n        else {\n          pv->next = co->next;\n        }\n        cookies->numcookies--;\n        freecookie(co);\n      }\n      else {\n        /*\n         * If this cookie has an expiration timestamp earlier than what we've\n         * seen so far then record it for the next round of expirations.\n         */\n        if(co->expires && co->expires < cookies->next_expiration)\n          cookies->next_expiration = co->expires;\n        pv = co;\n      }\n      co = nx;\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n/* Make sure domain contains a dot or is localhost. */\nstatic bool bad_domain(const char *domain, size_t len)\n{\n  if((len == 9) && strncasecompare(domain, \"localhost\", 9))\n    return FALSE;\n  else {\n    /* there must be a dot present, but that dot must not be a trailing dot */\n    char *dot = memchr(domain, '.', len);\n    if(dot) {\n      size_t i = dot - domain;\n      if((len - i) > 1)\n        /* the dot is not the last byte */\n        return FALSE;\n    }\n  }\n  return TRUE;\n}\n\n/*\n  RFC 6265 section 4.1.1 says a server should accept this range:\n\n  cookie-octet    = %x21 / %x23-2B / %x2D-3A / %x3C-5B / %x5D-7E\n\n  But Firefox and Chrome as of June 2022 accept space, comma and double-quotes\n  fine. The prime reason for filtering out control bytes is that some HTTP\n  servers return 400 for requests that contain such.\n*/\nstatic int invalid_octets(const char *p)\n{\n  /* Reject all bytes \\x01 - \\x1f (*except* \\x09, TAB) + \\x7f */\n  static const char badoctets[] = {\n    \"\\x01\\x02\\x03\\x04\\x05\\x06\\x07\\x08\\x0a\"\n    \"\\x0b\\x0c\\x0d\\x0e\\x0f\\x10\\x11\\x12\\x13\\x14\"\n    \"\\x15\\x16\\x17\\x18\\x19\\x1a\\x1b\\x1c\\x1d\\x1e\\x1f\\x7f\"\n  };\n  size_t len;\n  /* scan for all the octets that are *not* in cookie-octet */\n  len = strcspn(p, badoctets);\n  return (p[len] != '\\0');\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_add\n *\n * Add a single cookie line to the cookie keeping object. Be aware that\n * sometimes we get an IP-only host name, and that might also be a numerical\n * IPv6 address.\n *\n * Returns NULL on out of memory or invalid cookie. This is suboptimal,\n * as they should be treated separately.\n */\nstruct Cookie *\nCurl_cookie_add(struct Curl_easy *data,\n                struct CookieInfo *c,\n                bool httpheader, /* TRUE if HTTP header-style line */\n                bool noexpire, /* if TRUE, skip remove_expired() */\n                const char *lineptr,   /* first character of the line */\n                const char *domain, /* default domain */\n                const char *path,   /* full path used when this cookie is set,\n                                       used to get default path for the cookie\n                                       unless set */\n                bool secure)  /* TRUE if connection is over secure origin */\n{\n  struct Cookie *clist;\n  struct Cookie *co;\n  struct Cookie *lastc = NULL;\n  struct Cookie *replace_co = NULL;\n  struct Cookie *replace_clist = NULL;\n  time_t now = time(NULL);\n  bool replace_old = FALSE;\n  bool badcookie = FALSE; /* cookies are good by default. mmmmm yummy */\n  size_t myhash;\n\n  DEBUGASSERT(data);\n  DEBUGASSERT(MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT <= 255); /* counter is an unsigned char */\n  if(data->req.setcookies >= MAX_SET_COOKIE_AMOUNT)\n    return NULL;\n\n  /* First, alloc and init a new struct for it */\n  co = calloc(1, sizeof(struct Cookie));\n  if(!co)\n    return NULL; /* bail out if we're this low on memory */\n\n  if(httpheader) {\n    /* This line was read off an HTTP-header */\n    const char *ptr;\n\n    size_t linelength = strlen(lineptr);\n    if(linelength > MAX_COOKIE_LINE) {\n      /* discard overly long lines at once */\n      free(co);\n      return NULL;\n    }\n\n    ptr = lineptr;\n    do {\n      size_t vlen;\n      size_t nlen;\n\n      while(*ptr && ISBLANK(*ptr))\n        ptr++;\n\n      /* we have a <name>=<value> pair or a stand-alone word here */\n      nlen = strcspn(ptr, \";\\t\\r\\n=\");\n      if(nlen) {\n        bool done = FALSE;\n        bool sep = FALSE;\n        const char *namep = ptr;\n        const char *valuep;\n\n        ptr += nlen;\n\n        /* trim trailing spaces and tabs after name */\n        while(nlen && ISBLANK(namep[nlen - 1]))\n          nlen--;\n\n        if(*ptr == '=') {\n          vlen = strcspn(++ptr, \";\\r\\n\");\n          valuep = ptr;\n          sep = TRUE;\n          ptr = &valuep[vlen];\n\n          /* Strip off trailing whitespace from the value */\n          while(vlen && ISBLANK(valuep[vlen-1]))\n            vlen--;\n\n          /* Skip leading whitespace from the value */\n          while(vlen && ISBLANK(*valuep)) {\n            valuep++;\n            vlen--;\n          }\n\n          /* Reject cookies with a TAB inside the value */\n          if(memchr(valuep, '\\t', vlen)) {\n            freecookie(co);\n            infof(data, \"cookie contains TAB, dropping\");\n            return NULL;\n          }\n        }\n        else {\n          valuep = NULL;\n          vlen = 0;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Check for too long individual name or contents, or too long\n         * combination of name + contents. Chrome and Firefox support 4095 or\n         * 4096 bytes combo\n         */\n        if(nlen >= (MAX_NAME-1) || vlen >= (MAX_NAME-1) ||\n           ((nlen + vlen) > MAX_NAME)) {\n          freecookie(co);\n          infof(data, \"oversized cookie dropped, name/val %zu + %zu bytes\",\n                nlen, vlen);\n          return NULL;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Check if we have a reserved prefix set before anything else, as we\n         * otherwise have to test for the prefix in both the cookie name and\n         * \"the rest\". Prefixes must start with '__' and end with a '-', so\n         * only test for names where that can possibly be true.\n         */\n        if(nlen >= 7 && namep[0] == '_' && namep[1] == '_') {\n          if(strncasecompare(\"__Secure-\", namep, 9))\n            co->prefix |= COOKIE_PREFIX__SECURE;\n          else if(strncasecompare(\"__Host-\", namep, 7))\n            co->prefix |= COOKIE_PREFIX__HOST;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Use strstore() below to properly deal with received cookie\n         * headers that have the same string property set more than once,\n         * and then we use the last one.\n         */\n\n        if(!co->name) {\n          /* The very first name/value pair is the actual cookie name */\n          if(!sep) {\n            /* Bad name/value pair. */\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n            break;\n          }\n          strstore(&co->name, namep, nlen);\n          strstore(&co->value, valuep, vlen);\n          done = TRUE;\n          if(!co->name || !co->value) {\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n            break;\n          }\n          if(invalid_octets(co->value) || invalid_octets(co->name)) {\n            infof(data, \"invalid octets in name/value, cookie dropped\");\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n            break;\n          }\n        }\n        else if(!vlen) {\n          /*\n           * this was a \"<name>=\" with no content, and we must allow\n           * 'secure' and 'httponly' specified this weirdly\n           */\n          done = TRUE;\n          /*\n           * secure cookies are only allowed to be set when the connection is\n           * using a secure protocol, or when the cookie is being set by\n           * reading from file\n           */\n          if((nlen == 6) && strncasecompare(\"secure\", namep, 6)) {\n            if(secure || !c->running) {\n              co->secure = TRUE;\n            }\n            else {\n              badcookie = TRUE;\n              break;\n            }\n          }\n          else if((nlen == 8) && strncasecompare(\"httponly\", namep, 8))\n            co->httponly = TRUE;\n          else if(sep)\n            /* there was a '=' so we're not done parsing this field */\n            done = FALSE;\n        }\n        if(done)\n          ;\n        else if((nlen == 4) && strncasecompare(\"path\", namep, 4)) {\n          strstore(&co->path, valuep, vlen);\n          if(!co->path) {\n            badcookie = TRUE; /* out of memory bad */\n            break;\n          }\n          free(co->spath); /* if this is set again */\n          co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n          if(!co->spath) {\n            badcookie = TRUE; /* out of memory bad */\n            break;\n          }\n        }\n        else if((nlen == 6) &&\n                strncasecompare(\"domain\", namep, 6) && vlen) {\n          bool is_ip;\n\n          /*\n           * Now, we make sure that our host is within the given domain, or\n           * the given domain is not valid and thus cannot be set.\n           */\n\n          if('.' == valuep[0]) {\n            valuep++; /* ignore preceding dot */\n            vlen--;\n          }\n\n#ifndef USE_LIBPSL\n          /*\n           * Without PSL we don't know when the incoming cookie is set on a\n           * TLD or otherwise \"protected\" suffix. To reduce risk, we require a\n           * dot OR the exact host name being \"localhost\".\n           */\n          if(bad_domain(valuep, vlen))\n            domain = \":\";\n#endif\n\n          is_ip = Curl_host_is_ipnum(domain ? domain : valuep);\n\n          if(!domain\n             || (is_ip && !strncmp(valuep, domain, vlen) &&\n                 (vlen == strlen(domain)))\n             || (!is_ip && cookie_tailmatch(valuep, vlen, domain))) {\n            strstore(&co->domain, valuep, vlen);\n            if(!co->domain) {\n              badcookie = TRUE;\n              break;\n            }\n            if(!is_ip)\n              co->tailmatch = TRUE; /* we always do that if the domain name was\n                                       given */\n          }\n          else {\n            /*\n             * We did not get a tailmatch and then the attempted set domain is\n             * not a domain to which the current host belongs. Mark as bad.\n             */\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n            infof(data, \"skipped cookie with bad tailmatch domain: %s\",\n                  valuep);\n          }\n        }\n        else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"version\", namep, 7)) {\n          /* just ignore */\n        }\n        else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"max-age\", namep, 7)) {\n          /*\n           * Defined in RFC2109:\n           *\n           * Optional.  The Max-Age attribute defines the lifetime of the\n           * cookie, in seconds.  The delta-seconds value is a decimal non-\n           * negative integer.  After delta-seconds seconds elapse, the\n           * client should discard the cookie.  A value of zero means the\n           * cookie should be discarded immediately.\n           */\n          CURLofft offt;\n          const char *maxage = valuep;\n          offt = curlx_strtoofft((*maxage == '\\\"')?\n                                 &maxage[1]:&maxage[0], NULL, 10,\n                                 &co->expires);\n          switch(offt) {\n          case CURL_OFFT_FLOW:\n            /* overflow, used max value */\n            co->expires = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n            break;\n          case CURL_OFFT_INVAL:\n            /* negative or otherwise bad, expire */\n            co->expires = 1;\n            break;\n          case CURL_OFFT_OK:\n            if(!co->expires)\n              /* already expired */\n              co->expires = 1;\n            else if(CURL_OFF_T_MAX - now < co->expires)\n              /* would overflow */\n              co->expires = CURL_OFF_T_MAX;\n            else\n              co->expires += now;\n            break;\n          }\n        }\n        else if((nlen == 7) && strncasecompare(\"expires\", namep, 7)) {\n          char date[128];\n          if(!co->expires && (vlen < sizeof(date))) {\n            /* copy the date so that it can be null terminated */\n            memcpy(date, valuep, vlen);\n            date[vlen] = 0;\n            /*\n             * Let max-age have priority.\n             *\n             * If the date cannot get parsed for whatever reason, the cookie\n             * will be treated as a session cookie\n             */\n            co->expires = Curl_getdate_capped(date);\n\n            /*\n             * Session cookies have expires set to 0 so if we get that back\n             * from the date parser let's add a second to make it a\n             * non-session cookie\n             */\n            if(co->expires == 0)\n              co->expires = 1;\n            else if(co->expires < 0)\n              co->expires = 0;\n          }\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Else, this is the second (or more) name we don't know about!\n         */\n      }\n      else {\n        /* this is an \"illegal\" <what>=<this> pair */\n      }\n\n      while(*ptr && ISBLANK(*ptr))\n        ptr++;\n      if(*ptr == ';')\n        ptr++;\n      else\n        break;\n    } while(1);\n\n    if(!badcookie && !co->domain) {\n      if(domain) {\n        /* no domain was given in the header line, set the default */\n        co->domain = strdup(domain);\n        if(!co->domain)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n      }\n    }\n\n    if(!badcookie && !co->path && path) {\n      /*\n       * No path was given in the header line, set the default.  Note that the\n       * passed-in path to this function MAY have a '?' and following part that\n       * MUST NOT be stored as part of the path.\n       */\n      char *queryp = strchr(path, '?');\n\n      /*\n       * queryp is where the interesting part of the path ends, so now we\n       * want to the find the last\n       */\n      char *endslash;\n      if(!queryp)\n        endslash = strrchr(path, '/');\n      else\n        endslash = memrchr(path, '/', (queryp - path));\n      if(endslash) {\n        size_t pathlen = (endslash-path + 1); /* include end slash */\n        co->path = malloc(pathlen + 1); /* one extra for the zero byte */\n        if(co->path) {\n          memcpy(co->path, path, pathlen);\n          co->path[pathlen] = 0; /* null-terminate */\n          co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n          if(!co->spath)\n            badcookie = TRUE; /* out of memory bad */\n        }\n        else\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n      }\n    }\n\n    /*\n     * If we didn't get a cookie name, or a bad one, the this is an illegal\n     * line so bail out.\n     */\n    if(badcookie || !co->name) {\n      freecookie(co);\n      return NULL;\n    }\n    data->req.setcookies++;\n  }\n  else {\n    /*\n     * This line is NOT an HTTP header style line, we do offer support for\n     * reading the odd netscape cookies-file format here\n     */\n    char *ptr;\n    char *firstptr;\n    char *tok_buf = NULL;\n    int fields;\n\n    /*\n     * IE introduced HTTP-only cookies to prevent XSS attacks. Cookies marked\n     * with httpOnly after the domain name are not accessible from javascripts,\n     * but since curl does not operate at javascript level, we include them\n     * anyway. In Firefox's cookie files, these lines are preceded with\n     * #HttpOnly_ and then everything is as usual, so we skip 10 characters of\n     * the line..\n     */\n    if(strncmp(lineptr, \"#HttpOnly_\", 10) == 0) {\n      lineptr += 10;\n      co->httponly = TRUE;\n    }\n\n    if(lineptr[0]=='#') {\n      /* don't even try the comments */\n      free(co);\n      return NULL;\n    }\n    /* strip off the possible end-of-line characters */\n    ptr = strchr(lineptr, '\\r');\n    if(ptr)\n      *ptr = 0; /* clear it */\n    ptr = strchr(lineptr, '\\n');\n    if(ptr)\n      *ptr = 0; /* clear it */\n\n    firstptr = strtok_r((char *)lineptr, \"\\t\", &tok_buf); /* tokenize on TAB */\n\n    /*\n     * Now loop through the fields and init the struct we already have\n     * allocated\n     */\n    for(ptr = firstptr, fields = 0; ptr && !badcookie;\n        ptr = strtok_r(NULL, \"\\t\", &tok_buf), fields++) {\n      switch(fields) {\n      case 0:\n        if(ptr[0]=='.') /* skip preceding dots */\n          ptr++;\n        co->domain = strdup(ptr);\n        if(!co->domain)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        break;\n      case 1:\n        /*\n         * flag: A TRUE/FALSE value indicating if all machines within a given\n         * domain can access the variable. Set TRUE when the cookie says\n         * .domain.com and to false when the domain is complete www.domain.com\n         */\n        co->tailmatch = strcasecompare(ptr, \"TRUE\")?TRUE:FALSE;\n        break;\n      case 2:\n        /* The file format allows the path field to remain not filled in */\n        if(strcmp(\"TRUE\", ptr) && strcmp(\"FALSE\", ptr)) {\n          /* only if the path doesn't look like a boolean option! */\n          co->path = strdup(ptr);\n          if(!co->path)\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n          else {\n            co->spath = sanitize_cookie_path(co->path);\n            if(!co->spath) {\n              badcookie = TRUE; /* out of memory bad */\n            }\n          }\n          break;\n        }\n        /* this doesn't look like a path, make one up! */\n        co->path = strdup(\"/\");\n        if(!co->path)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        co->spath = strdup(\"/\");\n        if(!co->spath)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        fields++; /* add a field and fall down to secure */\n        /* FALLTHROUGH */\n      case 3:\n        co->secure = FALSE;\n        if(strcasecompare(ptr, \"TRUE\")) {\n          if(secure || c->running)\n            co->secure = TRUE;\n          else\n            badcookie = TRUE;\n        }\n        break;\n      case 4:\n        if(curlx_strtoofft(ptr, NULL, 10, &co->expires))\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        break;\n      case 5:\n        co->name = strdup(ptr);\n        if(!co->name)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        else {\n          /* For Netscape file format cookies we check prefix on the name */\n          if(strncasecompare(\"__Secure-\", co->name, 9))\n            co->prefix |= COOKIE_PREFIX__SECURE;\n          else if(strncasecompare(\"__Host-\", co->name, 7))\n            co->prefix |= COOKIE_PREFIX__HOST;\n        }\n        break;\n      case 6:\n        co->value = strdup(ptr);\n        if(!co->value)\n          badcookie = TRUE;\n        break;\n      }\n    }\n    if(6 == fields) {\n      /* we got a cookie with blank contents, fix it */\n      co->value = strdup(\"\");\n      if(!co->value)\n        badcookie = TRUE;\n      else\n        fields++;\n    }\n\n    if(!badcookie && (7 != fields))\n      /* we did not find the sufficient number of fields */\n      badcookie = TRUE;\n\n    if(badcookie) {\n      freecookie(co);\n      return NULL;\n    }\n\n  }\n\n  if(co->prefix & COOKIE_PREFIX__SECURE) {\n    /* The __Secure- prefix only requires that the cookie be set secure */\n    if(!co->secure) {\n      freecookie(co);\n      return NULL;\n    }\n c->newsession &&  /* clean session cookies */\n     !co->expires) {   /* this is a session cookie since it doesn't expire! */\n    freecookie(co);\n    return NULL;\n  }\n\n  co->livecookie = c->running;\n  co->creationtime = ++c->lastct;\n\n  /*\n   * Now we have parsed the incoming line, we must now check if this supersedes\n   * an already existing cookie, which it may if the previous We\n   * must also check that the data handle isn't NULL since the psl code will\n   * dereference it.\n   */\n  if(data && (domain && co->domain && !Curl_host_is_ipnum(co->domain))) {\n    const cookiehash(co->domain);\n  clist = c->cookies[myhash];\n  while(clist) {\n    if(strcasecompare(clist->name, co->name)) {\n      /* the names are identical */\n      bool matching_domains = FALSE;\n\n      if(clist->domain && co->domain) {\n        if(strcasecompare(clist->domain, co->domain))\n          /* The domains are identical */\n          matching_domains = TRUE;\n      }\n      else if(!clist->domain && !co->domain)\n        matching_domains = TRUE;\n\n      if(matching_domains && /* the domains were identical */\n         clist->spath && co->spath && /* both have paths */\n         clist->secure && !co->secure && !secure) {\n        size_t cllen;\n        const char *sep;\n\n        /*\n         * A non-secure cookie may not overlay an existing secure cookie.\n         * For an existing cookie \"a\" with path \"/login\", refuse a new\n         * cookie \"a\" with for example path \"/login/en\", while the path\n         * \"/loginhelper\" is ok.\n         */\n\n        sep = strchr(clist->spath + 1, '/');\n\n        if(sep)\n          cllen = sep - clist->spath;\n        else\n          cllen = strlen(clist->spath);\n\n        if(strncasecompare(clist->spath, co->spath, cllen)) {\n          infof(data, \"cookie '%s' for domain '%s' dropped, would \"\n                \"overlay an existing cookie\", co->name, co->domain);\n          freecookie(co);\n          return NULL;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    if(!replace_co && strcasecompare(clist->name, co->name)) {\n      /* the names are identical */\n\n      if(clist->domain && co->domain) {\n        if(strcasecompare(clist->domain, co->domain) &&\n          (clist->tailmatch == co->tailmatch))\n          /* The domains are identical */\n          replace_old = TRUE;\n      }\n      else if(!clist->domain && !co->domain)\n        replace_old = TRUE;\n\n      if(replace_old) {\n        /* the domains were identical */\n\n        if(clist->spath && co->spath &&\n           !strcasecompare(clist->spath, co->spath))\n          replace_old = FALSE;\n        else if(!clist->spath != !co->spath)\n          replace_old = FALSE;\n      }\n\n      if(replace_old && !co->livecookie && clist->livecookie) {\n        /*\n         * Both cookies matched fine, except that the already present cookie is\n         * \"live\", which means it was set from a header, while the new one was\n         * read from a file and thus isn't \"live\". \"live\" cookies are preferred\n         * so the new cookie is freed.\n         */\n        freecookie(co);\n        return NULL;\n      }\n      if(replace_old) {\n        replace_co = co;\n        replace_clist = clist;\n      }\n    }\n    lastc = clist;\n    clist = clist->next;\n  }\n  if(replace_co) {\n    co = replace_co;\n    clist = replace_clist;\n    co->next = clist->next; /* get the next-pointer first */\n\n    /* when replacing, creationtime is kept from old */\n    co->creationtime = clist->creationtime;\n\n    /* then free all the old pointers */\n    free(clist->name);\n    free(clist->value);\n    free(clist->domain);\n    free(clist->path);\n    free(clist->spath);\n\n    *clist = *co;  /* then store all the new data */\n\n    free(co);   /* free the newly allocated memory */\n    co = clist;\n  }\n\n  if(c->running)\n    /* Only show this when NOT reading the cookies from a file */\n    infof(data, \"%s cookie %s=\\\"%s\\\" for domain %s, path %s, \"\n          \"expire %\" CURL_FORMAT_CURL_OFF_T,\n          replace_old?\"Replaced\":\"Added\", co->name, co->value,\n          co->domain, co->path, co->expires);\n\n  if(!replace_old) {\n    /* then make the last item point on this new one */\n    if(lastc)\n      lastc->next = co;\n    else\n      c->cookies[myhash] = co;\n    c->numcookies++; /* one more cookie in the jar */\n  }\n\n  /*\n   * Now that we've added a new cookie to the jar, update the expiration\n   * tracker in case it is the This is always\n * called before any cookies are set. File may be NULL in which case only the\n * struct is initialized. Is file is \"-\" then STDIN is read.\n *\n * If 'newsession' is TRUE, discard all \"session cookies\" on read from file.\n *\n * Note that 'data' might be called as NULL pointer. We must make sure to run this\n       * after reading the file, and not on every cookie.\n       */\n      remove_expired(c);\n\n      if(handle)\n        fclose(handle);\n    }\n    data->state.cookie_engine = TRUE;\n  }\n  c->running = TRUE;          /* now, we're running */\n\n  return c;\n\nfail:\n  free(line);\n  /*\n   * Only clean up if we allocated it here, as the original could still be in\n   * use by a share handle.\n   */\n  if(!inc)\n    Curl_cookie_cleanup(c);\n  if(handle)\n    fclose(handle);\n  return NULL; /* out of memory */\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie_sort\n *\n * Helper function to sort cookies such that the longest path gets before the\n * shorter path. Path, domain and name lengths are considered in that order,\n * with the creationtime as the tiebreaker. The creationtime is guaranteed to\n * be unique per cookie, so we know we will get an ordering at that point.\n */\nstatic int cookie_sort(const void *p1, const void *p2)\n{\n  struct Cookie *c1 = *(struct Cookie **)p1;\n  struct Cookie *c2 = *(struct Cookie **)p2;\n  size_t l1, l2;\n\n  /* 1 - compare cookie path lengths */\n  l1 = c1->path ? strlen(c1->name) : 0;\n  l2 = c2->name ? strlen(c2->name) : 0;\n\n  if(l1 != l2)\n    return (l2 > l1) ? 1 : -1;\n\n  /* 4 - compare cookie creation time */\n  return (c2->creationtime > c1->creationtime) ? 1 : -1;\n}\n\n/*\n * cookie_sort_ct\n *\n * Helper function to sort cookies according to creation time.\n */\nstatic int cookie_sort_ct(const void *p1, const void *p2)\n{\n  struct Cookie *c1 = *(struct Cookie **)p1;\n  struct Cookie *c2 = *(struct Cookie **)p2;\n\n  return (c2->creationtime > c1->creationtime) ? 1 : -1;\n}\n\n#define CLONE(field)                     \\\n  do {                                   \\\n    if(src->field) {                     \\\n      d->field = strdup(src->field);     \\\n      if(!d->field)                      \\\n        goto fail;                       \\\n    }                                    \\\n  } while(0)\n\nstatic struct Cookie *dup_cookie(struct Cookie *src)\n{\n  struct Cookie *d = calloc(sizeof(struct Cookie), 1);\n  if(d) {\n    CLONE(domain);\n    CLONE(path);\n    CLONE(spath);\n    CLONE(name);\n    CLONE(value);\n    d->expires = src->expires;\n    d->tailmatch = src->tailmatch;\n    d->secure = src->secure;\n    d->livecookie = src->livecookie;\n    d->httponly = src->httponly;\n    d->creationtime = src->creationtime;\n  }\n  return d;\n\nfail:\n  freecookie(d);\n  return NULL;\n}\n\n/*\n * Curl_cookie_getlist\n *\n * For a given host and path, return a linked list of cookies that the client\n * should send to the server if used now. But when both hostname and cookie_domain are identical, the length check at line 145 returns TRUE. If the hostname were \".example.com\" with cookie_domain \"example.com\", the lengths differ (12 vs 11), so it would proceed to compare the domain portions.\n\nThe critical difference: the old code with `-1` would check hostname[0] = '.', accepting the match, while the new code checks hostname[1] = 'e', rejecting it. Since RFC 6265 specifies the cookie domain shouldn't have a leading dot, the validation needs to ensure proper subdomain boundaries—accepting exact matches and valid subdomains like \"www.example.com\" while rejecting malformed cases.\n\nThe vulnerability emerges when a hostname like \"xample.com\" could incorrectly match against a cookie domain \"ample.com\" because the index calculation no longer verifies the required dot separator between subdomain levels.\n\nWith hostname \"xample.com\" (length 10) and cookie_domain \"ample.com\" (length 9), the string comparison succeeds on the suffix. The old code checked `hostname[10 - 9 - 1] = hostname[0] = 'x'` for a dot boundary, correctly rejecting the match. The new code checks `hostname[10 - 9] = hostname[1] = 'm'`, which also happens to reject it in this case. However, the fundamental issue is that the new calculation points to the wrong position—it's checking the first character of the matched domain portion rather than the character immediately before it, which breaks the security invariant that requires a dot separator for valid subdomain matching. \"sub.example.com\" to match cookie_domain \"example.com\", but the new code incorrectly rejects it. The bug means the function only returns TRUE for exact hostname matches or an impossible condition, making it reject all subdomain cookies. This is a HIGH severity security defect that breaks cookie domain matching entirely. No, continue\n\nLine 147: Check the character at position `hostname_len - cookie_domain_len`\n- OLD: hostname[15 - 11 - 1] = hostname[3] = '.'\n- NEW: hostname[15 - 11] = hostname[4] = 'e'\n\nThe OLD code checks if there's a dot BEFORE the matched domain (at index 3 for \"sub.\"), which is correct.\nThe NEW code checks if the first character of the matched domain is a dot, which doesn't make sense.\n\nActually, let me recalculate the indices for \"sub.example.com\":\n- Index 0: 's'\n- Index 1: 'u'\n- Index 2: 'b'\n- Index 3: '.'\n- Index 4: 'e'\n- Index 5: 'x'\n- Index 6: 'a'\n- Index 7: 'm'\n- Index 8: 'p'\n- Index 9: 'l'\n- Index 10: 'e'\n- Index 11: '.'\n\n\n- Index 12: 'c'\n- Index 13: 'o'\n- Index 14: 'm'\n\nSo the old calculation correctly identifies the separator dot at index 3, while the new one points to 'e' at index 4. This breaks the validation logic—it's now checking if the domain itself starts with a dot instead of verifying a proper subdomain boundary. The result is that legitimate subdomains get rejected, creating a serious security flaw in cookie handling.\n\nThe impact extends beyond just rejecting valid cookies. When the function fails to match \"sub.example.com\" against \"example.com\", cookies won't be transmitted to legitimate subdomains. This could manifest as a denial-of-service scenario where users lose functionality across cookie-dependent sites. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_011Axdsb6h68awQpVmS5jERG","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I see a potential issue here. Looking at the code:```c\nfor(i = offset, si = offset; i < nread; i++, si++) {\n  if(k->upload_fromhere[i] == 0x0a) {\n    data->state.scratch[si++] = 0x0d;\n    data->state.scratch[si] = 0x0a;\n    // ...\n  }\n  else\n    data->state.scratch[si] = k->upload_fromhere[i];\n}\n```\n\nWait, there's an issue with the `si++` inside the if block. When we have a newline character:- i = some value, si = some value\n- We write 0x0d to scratch[si++] (which increments si)\n- Then we write 0x0a to scratch[si]\n- Then at the end of the loop, si++ is executed again in the for loop\n\nBut when we don't have a newline:\n- We write the character to scratch[si]\n- Then si++ is executed at the end of the loop\n\nSo in the newline case:\n1. scratch[si++] = 0x0d; (si is incremented before the assignment? No, post-increment, so it assigns then increments)\n2. scratch[si] = 0x0a; (now si is pointing to the next position because of the ++ in the first line)\n3. si++ at end of loop (si is incremented again)\n\nActually wait, let me re-read this more carefully:```c\ndata->state.scratch[si++] = 0x0d;\ndata->state.scratch[si] = 0x0a;\n```\n\nThe first line increments si AFTER the assignment, so:\n- scratch[si] = 0x0d\n- si is incremented\n- scratch[si] = 0x0a (using the new si)Then at the end of the loop, `si++` is executed again, so si is incremented once more.\n\n\nWhen encountering a newline, we're writing two bytes but incrementing si three times total—once in the post-increment on the first assignment, once more on the second line, and once in the loop increment. This creates a mismatch where si advances too far, skipping positions in the scratch buffer.\n\nLet me trace through this more carefully. For a newline character, scratch[si] gets 0x0d and si increments, then scratch[si+1] gets 0x0a, then the loop's si++ happens again. That means we've written two bytes but moved si forward by two positions, which leaves a gap. For regular characters, we write one byte and si advances by one. The issue is that the loop's increment is happening regardless of whether we've already manually incremented si inside the conditional. )\nfor i=2, si=3:\n  if(k->upload_fromhere[2] == 0x0a) -> 'b' != 0x0a -> false\n  else: scratch[3] = 'b'\n  (loop increment: i++, si++ -> i=3, si=4)\nfor i=3, si=4:\n  if(k->upload_fromhere[3] == 0x0a) -> 'c' != 0x0a -> false\n  else: scratch[4] = 'c'\n  (loop increment: i++, si++ -> i=4, si=5)\nfor i=4, si=5:\n  if(k->upload_fromhere[4] == 0x0a) -> '\\n' == 0x0a -> true\n    scratch[5++] = 0x0d\n\nContinuing through the loop, when we hit 'b' and 'c', they're not newlines so they just get copied directly to scratch. By the time we reach the second newline at position 4, si has already advanced to 5, and the carriage return gets written there.\n\nThe loop terminates once i reaches nread=5, leaving scratch = \"a\\r\\nbc\\r\\n\" with si=7. The core issue is that newlines expand to two characters (0x0d 0x0a) but the loop counter only increments by 1 per iteration, causing si to advance by 2 for newlines but only 1 for regular characters. This mismatch means the si increment in the loop doesn't properly account for the extra byte written when converting newlines.\n\nActually, reconsidering the mechanics: when processing \"a\\nb\" (3 input bytes), the output should be \"a\\r\\nb\" (4 bytes). The loop reads each input character once—'a' writes to scratch[0] with si becoming 1, '\\n' writes two bytes to scratch[1] and scratch[2] with si becoming 3, and 'b' writes to scratch[3] with si becoming 4. The si counter is advancing correctly because it increments after each write operation, whether that's one byte or two. then si is manually incremented by 1 inside the if (from the post-increment), then si++ at the loop end\n\nActually, let me re-count the post-increment:```c\ndata->state.scratch[si++] = 0x0d;\n```This post-increments si, so si is incremented by 1. Then the loop increments it again, so si is incremented by 2 total for newlines. But we write 2 characters, so the ratio is correct.\n\nFor non-newlines:```c\ndata->state.scratch[si] = k->upload_fromhere[i];\n```This doesn't increment si, then the loop increments it by 1.\n\nSo the issue is that for newlines, we're doing `si++` (post-increment in the assignment) which increments si to point to the next position, then we assign 0x0a to that position, then the loop increments si again.\n\nLet me trace through with \"a\\nb\" to see what happens. Starting with offset=0, si=0, i=0. First iteration processes 'a' at position 0, writing it to scratch[0], then incrementing both i and si to 1. Second iteration finds '\\n' at position 1, writes 0x0d to scratch[1] and increments si to 2 via the post-increment, then writes 0x0a to scratch[2]. the input is close to the buffer size, we could overflow. But the scratch buffer is allocated as `2 * data->set.upload_buffer_size`, and in the worst case where every byte is a newline, we'd need `nread * 2` characters. Since `nread` won't exceed `data->set.upload_buffer_size`, this fits within the allocated space. The function cookie_tailmatch() is used to verify that a hostname matches a cookie domain according to RFC 6265. The change removed the -1 offset from the boundary check, causing the code to verify the wrong character position. The code now checks if hostname[hostname_len - cookie_domain_len] (the first character of the matched domain) is a dot, instead of checking hostname[hostname_len - cookie_domain_len - 1] (the character before the domain match). Since domain names never start with a dot, this causes all legitimate subdomain matches to fail.
